<div id="review_178787193" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/178787193" />
    <a title="John Patrick Schutz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5676138-john-patrick-schutz"><img alt="John Patrick Schutz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308766611p2/5676138.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/178787193?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John Patrick Schutz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John Patrick Schutz" href="/user/show/5676138-john-patrick-schutz">John Patrick Schutz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5676138-john-patrick-schutz?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer178787193" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12216596508721749307">Quite possibly the best fiction I've read in a decade. I was always fond of Lois McMaster Bujold's "Vorkosigan Series" of Science-Fiction books - always rollicking good fun while having deep underlying issues that make the reader remember them long after all the action and humor have faded to the background... but when Bujold decided to turn her hand to grand fantasy she found even more.<br/><br/>The first book of this grouping, "The Curse of Chalion" grabbed me from the first page. As a fan of Tolkein wh</span>
  <span id="freeText12216596508721749307" style="display:none">Quite possibly the best fiction I've read in a decade. I was always fond of Lois McMaster Bujold's "Vorkosigan Series" of Science-Fiction books - always rollicking good fun while having deep underlying issues that make the reader remember them long after all the action and humor have faded to the background... but when Bujold decided to turn her hand to grand fantasy she found even more.<br /><br />The first book of this grouping, "The Curse of Chalion" grabbed me from the first page. As a fan of Tolkein who does NOT enjoy most of the imitators and pretenders that simply don't have the depth of plot, deeper issues, facility with language, and creation of a fully realized alternate reality I was thrilled to find Bujold a worthy successor to Tolkein and Ursula LeGuin.<br /><br />However, her second book in this loosely associated trio - "Paladin of Souls" took me from thrilled to astonishment. Not at all what one expects in a fantasy, our main character is a middle-aged noble woman, former Royina (Queen-Consort) and now "Dowager Royina" (mother of the current monarch). Only in her mid-forties, she is percieved as having served her purpose and is now no longer useful. In fact, she's considered slightly mad, though the reader will discover that assumption to be quite wrong. Troubled by a recurring dream, she embarks on what is obstensibly a religious pilgrimage, but is frankly an escape from those who would smother her with good intentions but slowly wring the life from her soul.<br /><br />What she finds is remarkable, inspiring and frightening. The book brought me, a grown 40-something man to tears of heartbreak, rage and overwhelming joy on several occassions - and I've heard other men, usually not the type, respond in the same way. It is not a surprise that this book won just about every award a science-fiction/fantasy novel CAN win. <br /><br />The follow-up third book "The Hallowed Hunt", is just as captivating as the first book "Chalion", and though it does not reach the soaring apex of the soul that "Paladin" acheives, it is in no way a letdown. It still has moments of staggering beauty and painful goodness, and brings us back to earth from the heights of the central novel.<br /><br />The grouping is so wonderful that after reading each at its initial publication (2001, 2003, 2005) I have since re-read them twice. The "finish" date is for my most recent reading. I recommend this series even to those who do not generally go for "Grand Fantasy" as this is true Grand Fantasy, NOT a "swords and sorcery" stamped-out rehashed pulp novel. The issues and emotions dealt with here are much more evolved and thoughtful than any pretender to Tolkein's throne could be. Dare I say it, her insight into emotions and motivations is better than that of Tolkein, who did not let us see into the very souls of his heroes and heroines the way Bujold bares the very core of her protagonists.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12216596508721749307" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2527508511" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2527508511" />
    <a title="Anthony" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4009947-anthony"><img alt="Anthony" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534088626p2/4009947.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2527508511?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anthony" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anthony" href="/user/show/4009947-anthony">Anthony</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780061748905" href="/book/show/10202499-paladin-of-souls">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4009947-anthony?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4009947-anthony?shelf=nebula-winners">nebula-winners</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4009947-anthony?shelf=hugo-winners">hugo-winners</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4009947-anthony?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4009947-anthony?shelf=locus-award-winners">locus-award-winners</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2527508511" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16012802135805290546">I had a rather puzzling experience with this novel. I find the quality of Bujold’s writing itself to be quite fluid, assured, and inventive; and I find her characters to be appealing, surprising, and full of intriguing quirks and depths. But somehow throughout this novel I felt kept at an arms’ length from feeling fully swept up by it. Then there were lovely, crystalline moments of emotional complexity and grace — the final scene between Ista and Goram was especially rich and moving — and I foun</span>
  <span id="freeText16012802135805290546" style="display:none">I had a rather puzzling experience with this novel. I find the quality of Bujold’s writing itself to be quite fluid, assured, and inventive; and I find her characters to be appealing, surprising, and full of intriguing quirks and depths. But somehow throughout this novel I felt kept at an arms’ length from feeling fully swept up by it. Then there were lovely, crystalline moments of emotional complexity and grace — the final scene between Ista and Goram was especially rich and moving — and I found myself wondering why other long stretches didn’t capture me as viscerally. <br /><br />At any rate, of the three Bujold novels I’ve read so far — The Curse of Chalion and Falling Free being the others — this was probably the most complex, although I enjoyed the overall moment-to-moment experience of reading Chalion the most. She’s an incredibly prolific writer, and much celebrated, and I remain impressed by her talents and intrigued enough by her work to continue to explore it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16012802135805290546" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1959603386?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike" href="/user/show/7608899-mike">Mike</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1959603386" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7351975199036188035">I love, LOVE the protagonist of this book. She's not a great warrior, or a skillful rogue, or a powerful wizard, or anything like that. She's not even a not-great warrior or a not-powerful wizard who grows more powerful as the story progresses.<br/><br/>She's a middle aged woman who really wants a vacation.<br/><br/>Ista was a fairly minor character in <i>Curse of Chalion</i>, albeit one who was hugely affected by the events of that book. Here, she's been restored to full sanity, and chafing at the restrictions of her (lo</span>
  <span id="freeText7351975199036188035" style="display:none">I love, LOVE the protagonist of this book. She's not a great warrior, or a skillful rogue, or a powerful wizard, or anything like that. She's not even a not-great warrior or a not-powerful wizard who grows more powerful as the story progresses.<br /><br />She's a middle aged woman who really wants a vacation.<br /><br />Ista was a fairly minor character in <i>Curse of Chalion</i>, albeit one who was hugely affected by the events of that book. Here, she's been restored to full sanity, and chafing at the restrictions of her (loving) caretakers who can't see that she no longer needs the caretaking. By sheer force of will, she bullies her way into going on a religious pilgrimage, and the story builds from there.<br /><br />She's a wonderfully cynical character, and this was a sedate, very adult story - much as the previous book was. While we don't see Cazavril at all (though he's mentioned plenty of times), this was an excellent addition to the world of Chalion, expanding and deepening the world.<br /><br />I still have trouble believing this is the same author who writes the action packed, overly clever Vorkosigan Saga, but I suppose she's just that talented.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7351975199036188035" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/121689679?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer121689679" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11849089385275370519">I'm going to say the same thing about this, the second volume of Bujold's Chalion trilogy (I suppose, I've only seen three titles, I have the third as "to read"), I'm surprised at how much I enjoyed it. I do try to reserve the "5 star" rating for books that I truly enjoy. Neither artistic writing, nor classic prose will I rate alone as 5 stars. I just got/get involved in these books. I care about the characters in them and am able to suspend belief and flow with the story.<br/><br/>Of late I've been (I be</span>
  <span id="freeText11849089385275370519" style="display:none">I'm going to say the same thing about this, the second volume of Bujold's Chalion trilogy (I suppose, I've only seen three titles, I have the third as "to read"), I'm surprised at how much I enjoyed it. I do try to reserve the "5 star" rating for books that I truly enjoy. Neither artistic writing, nor classic prose will I rate alone as 5 stars. I just got/get involved in these books. I care about the characters in them and am able to suspend belief and flow with the story.<br /><br />Of late I've been (I believe) a bit burned out and having trouble finding a book I really liked. I was becoming concerned that I might be...too hard on some. Whether that's true or not, I really like these books and give both of the volumes I've read so far my highest recommendation.<br /><br />That being said, let me say I'm surprised because these are not the type of books I might have thought of as the "type I generally like". Still the execution is wonderful. While they may be a bit more on the romantic side than I prefer, it somehow didn't/doesn't drive me away from these. They carry their romanticism without being maudlin. They manage to work in all the necessary plot points and do it as the book is carried by the characterization. <br /><br />So far excellent and I plan to get to the third as quickly as "may be" (LOL). Again, 5 stars, highest recommendation. </span>

<div id="review_686130297" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/686130297" />
    <a title="Rob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10743961-rob"><img alt="Rob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422270416p2/10743961.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/686130297?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rob" href="/user/show/10743961-rob">Rob</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/13640113-paladin-of-souls">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=author-female">author-female</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=audio-book">audio-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer686130297" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9871844027546454187"><b>Executive Summary:</b> A slow-paced but enjoyable fantasy novel that can mostly be read as a stand-alone.<br/><br/><b>Audio book:</b> This is my first novel read by Kate Reading. I have long heard she is a great narrator, and I would have to agree. She doesn't exactly do voices or anything but she does distinguish a bit between characters. She speaks clearly with good inflections and emotions.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br/>Right off the bat this novel is unique for me. The protagonist is a 40-something woman. That's never the case </span>
  <span id="freeText9871844027546454187" style="display:none"><b>Executive Summary:</b> A slow-paced but enjoyable fantasy novel that can mostly be read as a stand-alone.<br /><br /><b>Audio book:</b> This is my first novel read by Kate Reading. I have long heard she is a great narrator, and I would have to agree. She doesn't exactly do voices or anything but she does distinguish a bit between characters. She speaks clearly with good inflections and emotions.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br />Right off the bat this novel is unique for me. The protagonist is a 40-something woman. That's never the case for any of the fantasy books I've read.<br /><br />This book like it's predecessor <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61886.The_Curse_of_Chalion__Chalion___1_" title="The Curse of Chalion (Chalion, #1) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">The Curse of Chalion</a>, has a slow pace that somehow just works for me. The only other author/series I can think of that manages this is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25307.Robin_Hobb" title="Robin Hobb" rel="nofollow noopener">Robin Hobb</a>'s Edlerling books.<br /><br />I don't really remember the details of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61886.The_Curse_of_Chalion__Chalion___1_" title="The Curse of Chalion (Chalion, #1) by Lois McMaster Bujold" rel="nofollow noopener">The Curse of Chalion</a>, but that doesn't seem to matter. In fact I'd imagine you'd be able to read this book having skipped that one without issue. Not that I recommend it, because that book was also enjoyable.<br /><br />Most reviews I've read seem to indicate this is the best of the series. I found my enjoyment to be about the same. If anything distinguishes the two it's that this one doesn't focus on a male whose righting wrongs with his sword, but a woman who is doing it with her wits (and some help from the gods).<br /><br />I think this is one of those books you need to be in the right mood for. It's not a fast-paced, action packed sword and sorcery story. It's also not a politically charged struggle for power. Often times it seems that when strong woman are portrayed in fantasy, they are politically savvy nobility maneuvering for power.<br /><br />Instead we have a woman who decides she needs a journey. Not for adventure. Not for glory. Simply because she needs a break. Royina Ista has spent most of her life under a family curse or control of someone else. She just needs to get away. This doesn't seem to make sense to anyone else, so she does so under the guise of making a religious pilgrimage to pray for her daughter to have a grandson.<br /><br />Unfortunately for her (and fortunately the reader), the gods have other plans. Royina Ista is confronted with raiding soldiers, demons, sorcerers and a plot that threatens the safety of all of Chalion. There is a bit a of romance thrown in for good measure.<br /><br />All and all this is a well written and enjoyable fantasy story that is quite different from just about everything I read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9871844027546454187" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1946539947" />
    <a title="Kaitlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin"><img alt="Kaitlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481663259p2/19126246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1946539947?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaitlin" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin">Kaitlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007138494" href="/book/show/61883.Paladin_of_Souls">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1946539947" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15384012718419593098">This is technically the second book in this series, although it doesn't follow many of the characters from Curse of Chalion with the exception of Ista, the once-mad Royina, who is the main character of this book. <br/><br/>In this story we see that Ista, following the events in Curse of Chalion, doesn't really have any purpose in her life now. Both her children have gone and she's left surrounded by her mother's old court of stuffy and silly ladies quite unlike her. Although she's an older and sometimes b</span>
  <span id="freeText15384012718419593098" style="display:none">This is technically the second book in this series, although it doesn't follow many of the characters from Curse of Chalion with the exception of Ista, the once-mad Royina, who is the main character of this book. <br /><br />In this story we see that Ista, following the events in Curse of Chalion, doesn't really have any purpose in her life now. Both her children have gone and she's left surrounded by her mother's old court of stuffy and silly ladies quite unlike her. Although she's an older and sometimes bitter lady herself, she decides to undertake a holy pilgrimage in honour of her mother to escape her confines and hopefully discover a new purpose.<br /><br />Ista is a great character becuase she's had one of the hardest lives. Not only has she suffered through an immense curse but she's also been thought of as a mad lady for most of her life, set aside by her late husband early on, and looked down upon by many of the people supposed to love and care for her. She's bitter, she's well past her young prime, and yet she's fascinating to read about becuase she has life experience and she has snark and humour and a solid sense of determination.<br /><br />In this world magic and Gods go hand in hand and necromancy and daemons are all abundant (if you know where to look). Ista's journey allows her to encounter many different classes, races and sets of people and she also meets some who may be a whole lot more than they initially seem. <br /><br />What I really enjoy about Bujold's fantasy is that even though it's slow moving and subtle it works so well as a story and it feels comforting and exciting all at once. I think the different types of character that she chooses to portray really help her to stand out from other fantasy writers, and she does what she does so very masterfully too. <br /><br />Overall I really enjoyed this one and I am looking forward to reading more by Bujold in the near future. A solid 4.5*s from me and I have to say there were many excellent moments and characters within this one :)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15384012718419593098" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_730675846" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/730675846" />
    <a title="Jim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/695116-jim"><img alt="Jim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340192527p2/695116.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/730675846?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim" href="/user/show/695116-jim">Jim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780786182633" href="/book/show/296143.Paladin_of_Souls">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=3series">3series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=2fiction">2fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=1audio">1audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer730675846" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16292293419193084903">I read (listened to) this out of order, third instead of second. Not a big deal. The events take place soon after the first book, but the third is set centuries earlier, so doesn't impact it at all.<br/><br/>All three books had different readers. The first, told about a man was read by one. This one, about a woman, was read by one who did quite a good job.<br/><br/>Again, Bujold uses a damaged, ravaged soul as the focus of the story, except from the 'privileged' female perspective. Issa was simply a minor, piteous </span>
  <span id="freeText16292293419193084903" style="display:none">I read (listened to) this out of order, third instead of second. Not a big deal. The events take place soon after the first book, but the third is set centuries earlier, so doesn't impact it at all.<br /><br />All three books had different readers. The first, told about a man was read by one. This one, about a woman, was read by one who did quite a good job.<br /><br />Again, Bujold uses a damaged, ravaged soul as the focus of the story, except from the 'privileged' female perspective. Issa was simply a minor, piteous character previously, but events have freed her to find her own way again - sort of. The damn gods want a lot though &amp; this woman has to rise to meet their demands or be crushed.<br /><br />The nature of the gods &amp; demons is much discussed again. It's a very cool system that Bujold sets up with limits &amp; powers that are inventive &amp; even appalling at times. Very human-like without the monochromatic view of most fantasies. Yes, there is good &amp; evil, but sometimes its hard to tell one from the other, just like in real life. Other times it's obvious - there's definitely a goal - but the path getting through is quite twisty.<br /><br />Most of all, the characters are quite human. The heroes have their faults, the villains redeeming characteristics &amp; motivations. Even (especially?) saints are imperfect. The mix makes for a thoughtful, if action-packed &amp; memorable tale.<br /><br />I like the way Bujold handles horses in her books. I don't get the feeling that she's an expert on the subject the way <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8591.Janny_Wurts" title="Janny Wurts" rel="nofollow noopener">Janny Wurts</a> is, but she's certainly competent &amp; understands both their strengths &amp; frailties on a gut level. Horses get footsore just as riders occasionally get saddle sores. Wonderful! It's such a nice change of pace from the fantasy authors who think they're simply cars with hooves. Overall, this was a very 'real' fantasy firmly grounded in the realities of a Medieval society with all the little inconveniences that we no longer have to worry about &amp; so many authors forget about.<br /><br />I'm sorry to come to the end of these books. It's a great world that I will miss.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16292293419193084903" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2930750485" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2930750485" />
    <a title="Gabi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/84001290-gabi"><img alt="Gabi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593952673p2/84001290.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2930750485?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gabi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gabi" href="/user/show/84001290-gabi">Gabi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84001290-gabi?shelf=hugo_winners">hugo_winners</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84001290-gabi?shelf=locus_winners">locus_winners</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84001290-gabi?shelf=nebula_winners">nebula_winners</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2930750485" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6510099881337825547">This was the right book at the right time. These are not the 5 stars of an enthuiastic love at first sight, or a wow-moment. These are the 5 stars of the longlasting love that comes when the first impulses died down and reality is faced.<br/><br/>I felt absolutely comfortable with this story on nearly every level. Like in the first book Lois McMaster Bujold's prose is a perfect mix of lightfooted humor and a mature take on story and characters. It feels completely self-assured and therefore is able to dra</span>
  <span id="freeText6510099881337825547" style="display:none">This was the right book at the right time. These are not the 5 stars of an enthuiastic love at first sight, or a wow-moment. These are the 5 stars of the longlasting love that comes when the first impulses died down and reality is faced.<br /><br />I felt absolutely comfortable with this story on nearly every level. Like in the first book Lois McMaster Bujold's prose is a perfect mix of lightfooted humor and a mature take on story and characters. It feels completely self-assured and therefore is able to draw me right into the going-ons. Ista is a brilliant character and deviates refreshingly from your usual sword and sorcery heroes. She is strong without having to be badass, she is allowed to be insecure, yet she doesn't let others decide her life for her (not anymore). In the company of her young travel companions - each of them quite likeably drawn - she is more the motherly type without having to stand aside when the going gets tough. - In short: she is my dream character come true. It was simply a pleasure to follow her path and stand beside her in dire situations. Even the romance - which I so often don't like - was shown in a mature and still kind of cute way.<br /><br />The plot itself was full of interesting characters and twists, which I didn't see coming cause Bujold managed to get me fully immersed in the story so that I didn't watch it from the outside. This is the ideal story experience.<br /><br />I can understand why "Paladin of Souls" won the Hugo, the Nebula and the Locus award. I highly recommend it to everybody who is tired of the every same setup and heroes in Fantasy literature.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6510099881337825547" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2097516942" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2097516942" />
    <a title="Silvana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/666003-silvana"><img alt="Silvana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600533521p2/666003.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2097516942?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Silvana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Silvana" href="/user/show/666003-silvana">Silvana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6552070-paladin-of-souls">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/666003-silvana?shelf=fyeahfantasy">fyeahfantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/666003-silvana?shelf=kindle-google">kindle-google</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/666003-silvana?shelf=mine-mine-mine">mine-mine-mine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/666003-silvana?shelf=reading-with-friends">reading-with-friends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/666003-silvana?shelf=female-nonbinary-authors">female-nonbinary-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/666003-silvana?shelf=z-sff-2018-reading-challenge">z-sff-2018-reading-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/666003-silvana?shelf=z-sff-2018-female-challenge">z-sff-2018-female-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/666003-silvana?shelf=z-sl-sword-challenge-2018">z-sl-sword-challenge-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2097516942" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12678081490108223745">Finishing this book was not as fast as I thought. It was set in a more sedate pace than The Curse of Chalion. I know I said I missed Cazaril's POV a lot because he's funnier but actually Ista could be funny too with her dry remarks. Ista herself was a great character. It is not often we find a middle-age woman as a main character in any novels especially fantasy, which still has tendency to focus on teenage girls ready to fight the world and all that jazz. Maybe because I am past my teen years I</span>
  <span id="freeText12678081490108223745" style="display:none">Finishing this book was not as fast as I thought. It was set in a more sedate pace than The Curse of Chalion. I know I said I missed Cazaril's POV a lot because he's funnier but actually Ista could be funny too with her dry remarks. Ista herself was a great character. It is not often we find a middle-age woman as a main character in any novels especially fantasy, which still has tendency to focus on teenage girls ready to fight the world and all that jazz. Maybe because I am past my teen years I grow bored with those kinds of novels and want more mature ones. Well, this book delivers. Ista was perceptive, wise, thoughtful and yet she was human with emotions and desires. <br /><br />The plot in this book is so quite unpredictable. There were many twists and turns that keep me going. Even though the travelogue parts and also many, many expositions did not make this a page turner like the first book. <br /><br />The gods became more interesting. If you have followed my reviews for a while, I am not really fond of gods in fantasy. There were not many authors who could pull it off but Bujold is one of them. Every divine intervention was a pleasure to read. However, what made it even better can be described in this passage: "Men enslaved each other's bodies...the silent will of the soul was sacred and inviolable to the gods..." See, I liked that people had agencies, here.<br /><br />Now, the question is, should I read the third book? As far as I understand, it is a stand-alone. Or should I just try the other series in the World of Five Gods, i.e. Penric and Desdemona?</span>
  <a data-text-id="12678081490108223745" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_12793409" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Claire" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/746045-claire"><img alt="Claire" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1199652627p2/746045.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/12793409?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Claire" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Claire" href="/user/show/746045-claire">Claire</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/746045-claire?shelf=favorite-books-ever">favorite-books-ever</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/746045-claire?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer12793409" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11076707558162941101">One of my favorite books of all time. It took me a little while to transition into McMaster Bujold's fantasy novels (coming from her amazing enormous Miles Vorkosigan Sci-Fi series) but once I got into Chalion, I was hooked.<br/><br/>What I like best about McMaster Bujold is that her fantasy heroes (and heroines) are not straw-haired, starry-eyed farmers nor creatures out of myth or legend- she writes about tired adults, beaten down by the daily tragedies of life.<br/><br/>In this, her second book set in the kingdo</span>
  <span id="freeText11076707558162941101" style="display:none">One of my favorite books of all time. It took me a little while to transition into McMaster Bujold's fantasy novels (coming from her amazing enormous Miles Vorkosigan Sci-Fi series) but once I got into Chalion, I was hooked.<br /><br />What I like best about McMaster Bujold is that her fantasy heroes (and heroines) are not straw-haired, starry-eyed farmers nor creatures out of myth or legend- she writes about tired adults, beaten down by the daily tragedies of life.<br /><br />In this, her second book set in the kingdom of Chalion, the story follows 40-something Royina Ista, who has spent half of her life mured up in a tower after events in her early adulthood drove her insane. With the breaking of the curse, her mind is released but she is still imprisoned, this time by her loving family who endeavor to protect her from the world.<br /><br />Ista has no hopes or dreams for the future, and indeed only wishes the gods would leave her alone, because their action in her life nearly brought her to ruin: husband, friends, and son dead, remembered as an adulterer and a madwoman for having tried and failed so valiantly to save her king and her land.<br /><br />Indeed, she says bitterly that the only reason that she would not end her own life is that it would bring her face to face with the gods, whom she loathes with a bitter passion.<br /><br />Amazing, scintillating book. One of her best, one of my favorite books ever.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11076707558162941101" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText8448184725900958304" style="display:none">This book takes us three years after the events in The Curse of Chalion, where we follow dowager Royina Ista's adventures. Free from her madness, she seeks redemption through a pilgrimage. However, the gods meddle around and lead her to situations that involve ghosts from the past. Figuratively, don't worry.<br /><br />If you liked all the historical references from the Curse of Chalion, you will get a better picture of the world of Chalion, and a better understanding of the faith aspects as well.<br /><br />It is also different from most fantasy novels, for dealing with a 40-year old woman fighting through her regrets and bitterness from her youth. <br /><br />The only thing I didn't like was that deus ex machina rate, which was too high.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5347276495526499388">Being back to a familiar world and familiar characters – at least the ones in the opening chapters - made for a smooth and pleasant start.   <span id="freeText5347276495526499388" style="display:none">Being back to a familiar world and familiar characters – at least the ones in the opening chapters - made for a smooth and pleasant start. I had doubts about Ista as the MC, knowing her role in dy Lutez’s murder; while she never grew on me as much as Cazaril, she did manage to redeem herself. We got to meet interesting new people and, while I could guess at some upcoming turns of events, others did take me by surprise.<br /><br />My favourite aspect of the story was a much closer involvement of the gods. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The scene with the Father, short as it was, proved very emotional. But the Bastard stole the show: irreverent, full of tricks, with a twisted sense of humour – not unlike Loki, now that I think of it. No wonder I liked him best! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="5347276495526499388" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4On5EJrjw5Af5mK49jgWhDI621SFEI2thW96Z96l9GVgqfUJjdzFCMapaJ2jKXaiNFgo9uGrNstBHTYdj0aqqA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('54x9A5rcT2nuLP45JqZXObirQPFmDJuc+uRG7F6/hypnzHEajeNJ8Tdj9BxztzcfvsmzUwK3IPo+lgqWD1zZ5w==')})
  }
//]]>

But when his father and three sons in line for the throne are killed in an &quot;accident,&quot; he has no choice but to take his place as the only surviving rightful heir.\n\nEntirely unschooled in the art of court politics, he has no friends, no advisors, and the sure knowledge that whoever assassinated his father and brothers could make an attempt on his life at any moment.\n\nSurrounded by sycophants eager to curry favor with the naïve new emperor, and overwhelmed by the burdens of his new life, he can trust nobody. Amid the swirl of plots to depose him, offers of arranged marriages, and the specter of the unknown conspirators who lurk in the shadows, he must quickly adjust to life as the Goblin Emperor. All the while, he is alone, and trying to find even a single friend... and hoping for the possibility of romance, yet also vigilant against the unseen enemies that threaten him, lest he lose his <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10544902755964674333">Lois McMaster Bujold was born in 1949, the daughter of an engineering professor at Ohio State University, from whom she picked up her early interest in science fiction. She now lives in Minneapolis, and has two grown children. <br/><br/>Her fantasy from HarperCollins includes the award-winning Chalion series and the Sharing Knife tetralogy; her science fiction from Baen Books features the perennially bestse</span>
  <span id="freeText10544902755964674333" style="display:none">Lois McMaster Bujold was born in 1949, the daughter of an engineering professor at Ohio State University, from whom she picked up her early interest in science fiction. She now lives in Minneapolis, and has two grown children. <br /><br />Her fantasy from HarperCollins includes the award-winning Chalion series and the Sharing Knife tetralogy; her science fiction from Baen Books features the perennially bestselling Vorkosigan Saga. Her work has been translated into over twenty languages.<br /><br />A listing of her awards and nominations may be seen here:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.sfadb.com/Lois_McMaster_Bujold">http://www.sfadb.com/Lois_McMaster_Bu...</a><br /> <br />A listing of her interviews is here:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://vorkosigan.wikia.com/wiki/Author_Interviews">http://vorkosigan.wikia.com/wiki/Auth...</a><br /><br />An older fan-run site devoted to her work, The Bujold Nexus, is here:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.dendarii.com/">http://www.dendarii.com/</a><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10544902755964674333" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

In addition to the traitorous intrigues of villains, Cazaril and the Royesse Iselle, are faced with a sinister curse that hangs like a sword over the entire blighted House of Chalion and all who stand in their circle.
